Ibn Taymiyya's Redefinition of Good and Evil as Innate
Ibn Taymiyya defines hasan and qabih in terms of benefit and harm, asserting fitri knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Ibn Taymiyya defines hasan and qabih in terms of benefit and harm, and explain why he considers them knowable by fitra.

Core Idea
Good and evil are not arbitrary; they are rooted in the innate human disposition.

Ibn Taymiyya is challenging the view that moral concepts are purely rational or conventional. In this passage, he anchors the well-known propositions (mashhurat) about good and evil in the fitra, the innate disposition created by Allah. This move has profound implications for how we understand moral knowledge: it becomes certain and universal, not dependent on acquired reasoning or social consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms being defined
Locate the terms 'hasan' and 'qabih' in the Arabic. Notice that Ibn Taymiyya explicitly states what is meant (al-murad) by each term.
These are the definienda.
2
Extract the definitions
Hasan is defined as 'what is suitable and beneficial' (mulā'im nāfi'), and qabih as 'what is harmful and hurtful' (ḍārr mu'dhī). Write these definitions down.
The definitions are relational to human well-being.
3
Recognize the epistemological foundation
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that these definitions are not arbitrary but are rooted in the fitra. The fitra is the innate disposition that loves what is suitable and hates what harms. This makes the knowledge of good and evil necessary (ḍarūrī) and immediate.
Contrast this with the view that moral knowledge requires demonstration.
4
Compare to the standard Mantiq view of mashhurat
In classical logic, mashhurat are widely accepted opinions that may be false. Ibn Taymiyya elevates them to certainties because their principles are innate. Identify the shift: from probabilistic to certain.
This is a key point in his critique of Aristotelian logic.
5
Summarize the argument's structure
The passage moves from (a) the universal fact of fitra, to (b) the definitions of hasan and qabih based on that fitra, to (c) the conclusion that people know these propositions innately. Trace this flow.
This is not a syllogism but an epistemological claim based on anthropological observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الخامس : إن مبادىء هذه القضايا أمر ضروري في النفوس، فإنها مفطورة على حب ما يلائمها وبغض ما يضرها والمراد بالحَسَن ما يلائمها وبالقبيح ما يضرها . وإذا كانت مفطورة على حب هذا وبغض هذا فالمراد بقولنا حَسَن» أنه ملائم نافع، والمراد بقولنا «قبيح» أنه ضارّ مؤذ. وهذا أمر فطري فعلم أن الناس بفطرهم يعلمون هذه القضايا المشهورة بينهم .
The fifth type: The principles of these propositions are necessary in souls, for they are innately disposed to love what suits them and hate what harms them. What is meant by 'good' is what suits them, and by 'evil' is what harms them. Since they are innately disposed to love this and hate that, what is meant by our saying 'good' is that it is suitable and beneficial, and what is meant by our saying 'evil' is that it is harmful and hurtful. This is an innate matter, so it is known that people by their innate nature know these well-known propositions among them.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage defines the foundation of well-known (mashhurat) propositions. Ibn Taymiyya argues that their principles are necessary in human souls, because humans are created with an innate disposition (fitra) to love what is suitable and hate what harms. He then defines 'good' (hasan) as what is suitable and beneficial, and 'evil' (qabih) as what is harmful and hurtful. This is a definitional move: good and evil are not arbitrary but are rooted in the innate nature of man. The conclusion is that people know these well-known propositions by their fitra, not by acquired reasoning. This is a key epistemological claim in Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic, where he argues that foundational moral and practical knowledge is innate.

Al-Haqq Encompasses Moral Truths: Critique of Logicians' Denial
Author defines al-Haqq as including both factual and moral truth, critiquing logicians' denial of moral reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the logicians' claim that reason does not judge good and evil, by identifying the internal contradiction he exposes and explaining how 'al-Haqq' includes moral truths.

Core Idea
Truth includes justice and goodness; logicians who deny moral reason contradict their own universal consensus.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya expands the concept of al-Haqq beyond mere factual truth to encompass moral truths like justice and truthfulness. He argues that sound human reason naturally distinguishes good from evil, and this is confirmed by universal human agreement and by revelation. This directly contradicts the logicians' assertion that reason alone cannot judge morality. Let's unpack his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' claim under attack
Find where Ibn Taymiyya states the logicians' position: that reason alone does not judge good or evil. This is the target he will contradict.
The key phrase is 'لا بِحُسْن ولا بقبح'.
2
Trace Ibn Taymiyya's definition of al-Haqq
Note how he uses Quranic verses and juristic terminology to show that al-Haqq includes both existential correctness and moral rightness (e.g., valid worship vs. invalid).
He links 'bāṭil' to non-existence and invalidity in law and morality.
3
Locate the evidence for universal moral agreement
Identify the examples he gives: the goodness of truthfulness and justice, the ugliness of lying and injustice, and the common usage of 'haqq' for rights and just judgments.
He cites hadith and the story of Ka'b ibn Malik.
4
Extract the contradiction
Ibn Taymiyya explicitly says that acknowledging rational moral judgment contradicts the logicians' denial. Pinpoint the sentence: 'وهذا مناقض لقولهم'.
The contradiction is between their theoretical claim and their practical acknowledgment.
5
Assess the validity of the critique
Consider whether Ibn Taymiyya's own reasoning is sound: does the universal agreement of rational people prove that reason judges moral matters? Evaluate if the logicians could respond.
The critique relies on the fitra as a common foundation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه التاسع : كون الوجود كله مبنياً على الحق والعدل
ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿ ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللهَ هُوَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنَّ مَا يَدْعُونَ مِن دُونِهِ، هُوَ الباطل﴾ [سورة الحج : ٦٢] . وقوله: ﴿ فَذَلِكُمُ اللَّهُ رَبُّكُمُ الْحَقِّ فَمَاذَا بَعْدَ الْحَقِّ إِلَّا الضَّلَالُ﴾ [ سورة يونس : ٣٢]. ومعلوم أن ما عُبد من دونه موجود مخلوق، ولكن عبادته باطلة وضلال، فإنه ليس مستحقاً لأن يُعبَد . فليست عبادته حقاً بل باطلاً، وهو باطل، لأن المقصود منه بالعبادة معدوم. ولهذا يقول الفقهاء بَطَلت العبادة»، و «بَطَل العقد». وقد قال تعالى : ( وَلَا يُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَلَكُمْ ﴾ [سورة محمد : ۳۳] . والإبطال ضد الإحقاق. وقال ﴿ تعالى: (الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا وَصَدُّوا عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَضَلَّ أَعْمَلَهُمْ لا وَالَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّرَاحَت وَمَامَنُوا بِمَا نزلَ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَهُوَ الْحَقُّ مِن رَّنِهِمْ كَفَرَ عَنْهُمْ سَيِّئَاتِهِمْ وَأَصْلَحَ بالهم يا ذلِكَ بِأَنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَتَّبَعُوا الْبَاطِلَ وَأَنَّ بَالَهُمْ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا اتَّبِعُوا الحَقَّ مِن رَّبِّهِمْ ﴾ [سورة محمد : ۱ - ۳ ] .
وقد بين الله أن الأعمال السيئة القبيحة باطلة في مثل قوله: ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَعْمَلُهُمْ كَسَرَابِ بِقِيعَةٍ يَحْسَبُهُ الظَّمْثَانُ مَاءً حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءَهُ لَمْ يَجِدْهُ شَيْئًا وَوَجَدَ اللَّهَ عِندَهُ فَوَقَنَهُ أن الأعمال مسَابَهُ وَاللَّهُ سَرِيعُ الْحِسَابِ أَوْ كَظُلُمَةٍ فِي بَحْرٍ لُبّي يَغْشَهُ مَوْجٌ ) الآية [سورة النور : ۳۹ - ٤٠] . فهذا الثاني مَثَل لما يصدر عن الجهل البسيط ، والأولُ للجهل المركَّب ۱ وقال تعالى: ﴿ يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا لَا تُبْطِلُوا صَدَقَتِكُم بِالْمَنِ وَالْأَذَى كَالَّذِي يُنفِقُ مَالَهُ رِئَاءَ النَّاسِ وَلَا يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ فَمَثَلُهُ كَمَثَلِ صَفْوَانٍ عَلَيْهِ تُرَابٌ فَأَصَابَهُ وَابِلٌ فَتَرَكَهُ صَلَدًا لا يَقْدِرُونَ عَلَى شَيْءٍ مِمَّا كَسَبُوا ﴾ [سورة البقرة: ٢٦٤]. فهذا مثل إبطال العمل بالمنّ والأذى، وبالرياء والكفر. والمقصود أنها لم تبق نافعة بخلافِ العمل الحق المحمود فإنه نافع ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَقَدِمْنَا إِلَى مَا عَمِلُوا مِنْ عَمَلٍ فَجَعَلْنَاهُ هَبَاءُ مَّنثُورًا [سورة الفرقان : ۲۳] . وبالجملة فما ذكروه تصريح منهم بأن العقل يميز بين الجميل والقبيح، وأن العاقل يلتذ بالجميل ويتألم بالقبيح، وأن الجميل كمال وخير للقوّة العاقلة من حيث هي بأن العقل يقضي بذلك. وهذا مناقض لقولهم : إن العقل بمجرده لا يقضي في أمثال هذا بشيء ـ لا بِحُسْن ولا بقبح». وهكذا تناقضوا في نفس الوهميات كما سنذكره إن شاء الله . وسبب ذلك أنهم تارةً يقولون بموجب الفطرة السليمة فيكون كلامهم صحيحاً، وتارة يقولون بمقتضى الفطرة الفاسدة التي قد فَسَدت بالاعتقادات الفاسدة فيقولون باطلاً .
وهذه القضايا التي اتفقت الأمم عليها مثل حسن الصدق والعدل وقبح الظلم والكذب داخلة في مسمى «الحق» كما تقدم - في كلام الله ورسوله، وكذلك كلام العقلاء قاطبة - يسمون هذا كله «حقاً». ويقولون لصاحب الدين: «له عليه حق» و أعطيه حقه». وإذا حكم بينهما بعدل وقسم بإنصاف يقولون هذا حق»، وإن حكم بخلاف ذلك يقولون هذا ظلم وجور». وإذا لم يكن له عنده شيء قالوا : «ما له حق، بل هو يدعي الباطل فيسمون الصدق حقاً) والكذب «باطلاً»، كما في كلام الله ورسوله . قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : «إن لصاحب الحق مقالاً» ، وفي لفظ : «إن لصاحب الحق اللسان واليد». وقال لكعب بن مالك لما طلب غَرِيمَه : أي كعب! ضَعِ الشَّطْر» قال «قد فعلت يا رسول الله ! » . قال : قم فاقضه» .
وذلك لأن الأمور الحسنة تتضمن أمراً موجوداً ماضياً ومستقبلاً، ففيها وجود وكمال الوجود. والأمور القبيحة تتضمن عدماً ماضياً أو مستقبلاً، ففيها نفي الوجود أو كمال الوجود . فإن كان موجوداً كان العلم بوجوده حقاً مطابقاً له، والأخبار عن وجوده كذلك . وأما الكذب المتضمن نفيه والجهلُ الذي [ هو ] عدم العلم به فهو عدم علم وعدم قول حق، بل الكذب من جنس الجهل المركب وأيضاً، العلم كمال وجود والصدقُ كمال وجود، والجهل والكذب صفة نقص .
Station Four - Aspect Nine: That all existence is based on truth and justice. And from it is His saying, the Most High: 'That is because Allah is the Truth, and that what they invoke besides Him is falsehood' [Surah al-Hajj: 62]. And His saying: 'That is Allah, your Lord, the Truth. So what after the Truth except misguidance?' [Surah Yunus: 32]. And it is known that what is worshipped besides Him is existent, created, but worshipping it is falsehood and misguidance, for it is not deserving of worship. So its worship is not truth but falsehood, and it is falsehood, because the purpose of worship from it is non-existent. Hence the jurists say: 'The act of worship becomes invalid (batalat al-‘ibada)', and 'the contract becomes void (batal al-‘aqd)'. And the Most High said: 'And do not invalidate your deeds' [Surah Muhammad: 33]. And invalidation (al-ibtal) is the opposite of making true (al-ihqaq). And the Most High said: 'Those who disbelieve and avert [people] from the way of Allah – He will waste their deeds. And those who believe and do righteous deeds and believe in what has been sent down upon Muhammad – and it is the truth from their Lord – He will remove from them their misdeeds and amend their condition. That is because those who disbelieve follow falsehood, and those who believe follow the truth from their Lord' [Surah Muhammad: 1-3]. And Allah has made clear that evil, ugly deeds are false in such as His saying: 'And those who disbelieve – their deeds are like a mirage in a lowland which the thirsty supposes is water, until when he comes to it he finds it nothing, and finds Allah before him, and He pays him in full his account. And Allah is swift in account. Or like darkness within a deep sea which is covered by waves...' the verse [Surah an-Nur: 39-40]. So this second is a parable for what arises from simple ignorance, and the first for compound ignorance. And the Most High said: 'O you who have believed, do not invalidate your charities with reproach and injury, like one who spends his wealth [only] to be seen by people and does not believe in Allah and the Last Day. His example is that of a [large] smooth stone upon which is dust and is hit by a downpour that leaves it bare. They are unable [to keep] anything of what they have earned' [Surah al-Baqara: 264]. This is a parable for invalidating deeds with reproach and injury, and with hypocrisy and disbelief. And the point is that they do not remain beneficial, contrary to the true, praiseworthy deed which is beneficial. And from it is His saying: 'And We will approach what they have done of deeds and make them as scattered dust' [Surah al-Furqan: 23]. In summary, what they mention is a declaration from them that reason distinguishes between the beautiful and the ugly, and that the rational person takes pleasure in the beautiful and is pained by the ugly, and that the beautiful is perfection and good for the rational faculty as such, because reason judges that. And this contradicts their statement: 'Reason alone does not judge in such matters – neither good nor evil.' Thus they contradict themselves even in the imaginary matters, as we will mention if Allah wills. And the reason for that is that sometimes they speak according to sound innate disposition (fitra) and their speech is correct, and sometimes they speak according to corrupt innate disposition that has been corrupted by corrupt beliefs, and thus they speak falsehood. And these propositions upon which the nations agree, such as the goodness of truthfulness and justice and the ugliness of injustice and lying, are included in the meaning of 'truth' (al-Haqq) as previously stated – in the speech of Allah and His Messenger, and likewise the speech of all rational people – they call all of this 'truth'. They say concerning the holder of a right: 'He has a right upon him' and 'Give him his right.' And if one judges between them with justice and divides with fairness they say 'This is truth', and if one judges otherwise they say 'This is injustice and tyranny.' And if there is nothing due to him, they say: 'He has no right; rather he claims falsehood.' So they call truthfulness 'truth' and lying 'falsehood', as in the speech of Allah and His Messenger. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed the holder of a right has a say,' and in another wording: 'Indeed the holder of a right has a tongue and a hand.' And he said to Ka‘b ibn Malik when he sought his creditor: 'O Ka‘b! Remit half of it.' He said: 'I have done so, O Messenger of Allah!' He said: 'Get up and pay him.' And that is because good deeds entail an existent matter, past and future; so in them is existence and perfection of existence. And evil deeds entail a non-existence, past or future; so in them is negation of existence or perfection of existence. So if something is existent, knowledge of its existence is truth (haqq) corresponding to it, and reporting of its existence is likewise. As for lying which entails its negation, and ignorance which is absence of knowledge of it, that is ignorance and absence of truthful speech; rather, lying is of the genus of compound ignorance. Also, knowledge is perfection of existence and truthfulness is perfection of existence, while ignorance and lying are attributes of deficiency.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya on the concept of 'al-Haqq' (truth/right/reality) and its implications for the logicians' denial of rational moral judgment. He begins by citing Quranic verses that establish Allah as the Truth and contrast truth with falsehood (bāṭil). He notes that objects of worship besides Allah are existent creatures, but worshipping them is false because they are not deserving; the intended purpose is non-existent. He connects this to juristic terminology: acts of worship and contracts are declared invalid (bāṭil) when they lack proper basis. Thus 'truth' (ḥaqq) implies existence and correctness, while 'falsehood' implies non-existence or invalidity. He then expands to show that evil deeds are described as false in the Quran, citing parables of deeds like a mirage or dust on a rock. The conclusion is that reason distinguishes between beautiful and ugly, and the beautiful is perfection and good for the rational faculty. This contradicts the logicians' claim that reason alone does not judge good or evil. Ibn Taymiyya diagnoses the source of this contradiction: they sometimes follow sound natural disposition (fiṭra) and speak rightly, but other times follow corrupt fiṭra and speak falsely. He then brings forward the universal consensus of nations on moral truths like the goodness of truthfulness and justice and the ugliness of injustice and lying. These are all included in the meaning of 'ḥaqq', as evidenced by common parlance: granting someone his right, just judgments, and labeling claims as true or false. He supports this with prophetic hadith about the creditor's right and the story of Ka‘b ibn Malik. Finally, he provides an ontological analysis: good deeds involve existence and perfection, while evil deeds involve non-existence or deficiency. True knowledge and truthful speech correspond to existence; falsehood and ignorance involve negation or absence. Thus truth is linked to existence and perfection, falsehood to non-existence and deficiency. This underscores his critique: the logicians' own acknowledgment of moral universals contradicts their denial of rational ethical judgment.

Key Terms
الحق (al-Haqq): Truth, reality, or right; includes both factual truth and moral rightness; what is existent and deserving, as opposed to falsehood (bāṭil). In this passage, it encompasses moral truths like justice and truthfulness. [Note: No significant shift; this term is stable across the tradition, though Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes its moral dimension against the logicians' narrow epistemic use.]
الباطل (al-Bāṭil): Falsehood; that which is non-existent, invalid, or morally wrong; includes lies, injustice, and invalid acts of worship or contracts. [Note: No significant shift; standard usage.]
الجميل والقبيح (al-jamīl wa al-qabīḥ): The beautiful and the ugly; moral categories of good and evil as discerned by reason and innate disposition (fiṭra). [Note: In falsafa tradition, these are often objective attributes; Ibn Taymiyya grounds them in fiṭra and revelation, critiquing the Ash‘arī and logician denial of rational moral judgment.]
الفطرة (al-fiṭra): Innate disposition or natural constitution; when sound, it allows correct moral judgment; when corrupted by false beliefs, it leads to falsehood. [Note: Ibn Taymiyya uses fiṭra as an epistemological foundation, different from its usage in kalām as original human nature.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in this passage, what is the relationship between the logicians' claim that reason does not judge good and evil and their acknowledgement that rational people agree on the goodness of truthfulness and the ugliness of lying?
A) They are consistent because moral judgments are based on revelation alone.
B) They are contradictory because they admit that reason does make such judgments in practice.
C) They are complementary because reason judges only theoretical matters, not practical ones.
D) They are irrelevant because the logicians never acknowledged such agreement.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that the logicians' own admission of universal moral agreement contradicts their denial of rational moral judgment, and that al-Haqq inherently includes moral truths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the internal contradiction in the following statement of a hypothetical logician: 'Reason cannot judge moral matters, but all rational people agree that justice is good and injustice is evil.' Explain how Ibn Taymiyya would respond, using his argument from this lesson.
?
Find a verse or hadith not mentioned in this passage that supports the claim that moral truths are part of al-Haqq. Explain its relevance to Ibn Taymiyya's overall argument.

What Is Mantiq?
advanced
5 min
Critique of Relativity of Propositional Classifications
Critique of the relativity of propositional classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the burhani/jadali/khitabi distinction is relative and evaluate why this undermines the claim that logic is a universal tool for distinguishing truth.

Core Idea
If a proposition's classification depends on the knower, it cannot be an intrinsic standard for truth.

Ibn Taymiyya targets a foundational claim of the logicians: that propositions can be sorted into burhani (demonstrative), jadali (dialectical), and khitabi (rhetorical) based on their epistemic character. He argues that these categories are not fixed features of the propositions themselves but are relative to the person using or conceding them. This relativity, he contends, prevents the logicians' method from serving as a universal criterion for truth, unlike the method of the prophets which provides common benefit for all humanity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proposition types
Find in the passage how the logicians define burhani (known to the user of evidence), jadali (conceded by the opponent), and khitabi (widely accepted or probable). Note that each definition refers to a relation to a person, not the proposition itself.
Ibn Taymiyya states these definitions at the beginning.
2
Analyze the 'relative and accidental' claim
Ibn Taymiyya says these are 'nisab wa idafat 'arida' (relative and accidental attributes). Explain why: a proposition can be true without anyone knowing it, and it can be jadali/khitabi while still true in itself. Therefore, the categories do not describe the proposition's intrinsic nature.
Contrast with essential attributes that a proposition has regardless of knowers.
3
Contrast with prophetic method
Ibn Taymiyya says the prophets reported propositions that are true in themselves and provided methods ('turuq 'ilmiyya') that benefit all people. How does this avoid the relativity problem? Because the truth is determined by correspondence to reality, not by a knower's awareness.
The prophetic method provides a 'scale' (mizan) for truth that is universal.
4
Evaluate the objection and response
Ibn Taymiyya anticipates an objection: logicians might admit that burhaniyya is relative (what you know is burhani for you). He responds that if materials of demonstration are not fixed, then the whole 'material' part of logic collapses. Explain this consequence.
If materials are left unspecified, logic becomes useless as a universal tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث عشر: أن يقال: كون القضية برهانية معناه عندهم أنها معلومة للمستدل بها، وكونها جدلية معناه كونها مسلمة، وكونها خطابية معناه كونها مشهورة أو مقبولة أو مظنونة. وجميع هذه الفروق هي نسب وإضافات عارضة للقضية، ليس فيها ما هو صفة ملازمة لها، فضلاً عن أن تكون ذاتية لها على أصلهم، بل ليس فيها ما هو صفة لها في نفسها. بل هذه صفات نسبية باعتبار شعور الشاعر بها. ومعلوم أن القضية قد تكون حقاً والإنسان لا يشعر بها، فضلاً أن يظنها أو يعلمها. وكذلك قد تكون خطابية أو جدلية وهي حق في نفسها، بل قد تكون برهانية أيضاً كما قد سلموا ذلك. وإذا كان كذلك فالرسل صلوات الله عليهم أخبروا بالقضايا التي هي حق في نفسها إخبار الرسل لا تكون كذباً باطلاً قط. وبينوا من الطرق العلمية التي يعرف بها صدق تلك القضايا ما هو مشترك ينتفع به جنس بني آدم، وهذا هو العلم النافع للناس. وأما هؤلاء المتفلسفة فلم يسلكوا هذا المسلك، بل سلكوا في القضايا الأمر النسبي، فجعلوا البرهانيات ما علمه المستدل، وغير ذلك لم يجعلوه برهانيات وإن علمه مستدل آخر. والجدليات ما سلمه المنازع وإن لم يسلمه غيره. وعلى هذا فتكون من البرهانيات عند إنسان وطائفة ما ليس من البرهانيات عند إنسان وطائفة أخرى. فلا يمكن أن تحد القضايا العلمية بحد جامع مانع، بل تختلف باختلاف أحوال من علمها ومن لم يعلمها. حتى إن أهل الصناعات عند أهل كل صناعة من القضايا التي يعلمونها ما لا يعلمها غيرهم. وحينئذ فيمتنع أن تكون طريقهم مميزة للحق من الباطل والصدق من الكذب باعتبار ما هو الأمر عليه في نفسه، ويمتنع أن تكون منفعتها مشتركة بين الآدميين. طريقهم بخلاف طريقة الأنبياء، فإنهم أخبروا بالقضايا الصادقة التي تفرق بين الحق والباطل بها الناس. والصدق والكذب، فكل ما ناقض الصدق فهو كذب وكل ما ناقض الحق فهو باطل. فلهذا جعل الله ما أنزله من الكتاب حاكماً بين الناس فيما اختلفوا فيه. وأنزل أيضاً الميزان، وهو ما يوزن به ويعرف به الحق من الباطل، ولكل حق ميزان يوزن به، بخلاف ما فعله الفلاسفة المنطقيون، فإنه لا يمكن أن يكون هادياً للحق، ولا مفرقاً بين الحق والباطل، ولا هو ميزان يعرف بها الحق من الباطل. وأما المتكلمون فما كان في كلامهم موافقاً لما جاءت به الأنبياء فهو منه، وما خالفه فهو من البدع الباطلة شرعاً وعقلاً. فإن قيل: نحن نجعل البرهانيات إضافية، فكل ما علمه الإنسان بمقدماته فهو برهاني عنده وإن لم يكن برهانياً عند غيره. قيل: لم يفعلوا ذلك. فإن من سلك هذا السبيل لم يجد مواد البرهان في أشياء معينة مع إمكان علم كثير من الناس لأمور أخر بغير تلك المواد المعينة التي عينوها. وإذا قالوا نحن لا نعين المواد، فقد بطل أحد أجزاء المنطق. وهو المطلوب.
The thirteenth aspect: It is said: For them, a proposition being burhani means it is known to the one using it as evidence; being jadali means it is conceded; being khitabi means it is widely accepted, or accepted from a trustworthy source, or probable. All these distinctions are relative and accidental attributes of the proposition, none of which are necessary attributes of it, let alone essential to it according to their own principles; rather, they are not attributes of it in itself. Rather, these are relative attributes based on the awareness of the one aware of it. It is known that a proposition may be true while a person is not aware of it, let alone supposing it or knowing it. Likewise, it may be khitabi or jadali while being true in itself; indeed, it may even be burhani, as they themselves have conceded. If this is so, then the Messengers (peace be upon them) informed of propositions that are true in themselves; the reports of the Messengers are never lying falsehood. And they explained from the scientific methods by which the truth of those propositions is known what is commonly beneficial to all of humanity, and this is the beneficial knowledge for people. As for these philosophers, they did not take this path; rather, they took the path of relativity in propositions, making burhani what the one using evidence knows, and not making others burhani even if another user of evidence knows them. And jadali is what the opponent concedes, even if others do not concede it. On this basis, what is burhani for one person or group may not be burhani for another person or group. Therefore, scientific propositions cannot be defined by a comprehensive exclusive definition; rather, they vary according to the states of those who know them and those who do not. Even the practitioners of each craft have propositions that they know which others do not. Consequently, their method cannot distinguish truth from falsehood and sincerity from lying in terms of what it is in itself, nor can its benefit be common among humans. Their method is contrary to the method of the prophets, for they informed of true propositions by which people distinguish truth from falsehood. Sincerity and falsehood: whatever contradicts sincerity is falsehood, and whatever contradicts truth is falsehood. Therefore, God made what He revealed of the Book as a judge between people in what they differ. He also revealed the scale, which is that by which truth is distinguished from falsehood, and every truth has a scale by which it is weighed, unlike what the logical philosophers did, for it cannot be a guide to truth, nor a distinguisher between truth and falsehood, nor is it a scale by which truth is known from falsehood. As for the theologians, what in their speech agrees with what the prophets brought is from them, and what contradicts it is heretical innovation, invalid by law and reason. If it is said: We make burhaniyya relative; whatever a person knows through its premises is burhani for him, even if not burhani for others. It is said: They did not do that. For whoever takes this path will not find the materials of demonstration in specific things, given the possibility of many people knowing other things by methods other than those specific materials they designated. And if they say we do not specify the materials, then one part of logic is invalidated. That is what was sought.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument against the logicians' classification of propositions into burhani (demonstrative), jadali (dialectical), and khitabi (rhetorical). Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating the definitions according to the logicians: a burhani proposition is one known to the person using it as evidence; a jadali proposition is one conceded by the opponent; a khitabi proposition is one widely accepted or accepted from a trustworthy source or probable. He then points out that all these distinctions are relative and accidental, not essential attributes of the propositions themselves. They depend on the awareness of the knower, not on the intrinsic truth of the proposition. A proposition can be true even if no one knows it, and it can be khitabi or jadali while being true in itself, or even burhani. Therefore, the logicians' classification cannot serve as a universal criterion for truth. The prophets, on the other hand, conveyed true propositions and provided methods by which people can distinguish truth from falsehood, methods beneficial to all humanity. The philosophers' method is relative; what is burhani for one may not be for another, so it cannot be a common judge. God sent the Book and the Scale (balance) as a judge between people. Ibn Taymiyya then addresses an objection: the logicians might claim that burhaniyya is indeed relative, so the classification is based on the knower's knowledge. He responds that if they do not specify the materials of demonstration, then one part of logic (the study of materials) becomes invalid. Thus, the logicians' method fails to provide a universal standard for truth.

Key Terms
البرهانية
الجدلية
الخطابية
النسبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, why can the logicians' classification of propositions (burhani, jadali, khitabi) not serve as a universal criterion for distinguishing truth from falsehood?
A) Because these categories are based on the intrinsic nature of propositions.
B) Because these categories are relative to the knower or debater, and not intrinsic to the proposition itself.
C) Because prophets do not use these categories.
D) Because the logicians disagree among themselves.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's core insight: if a proposition's classification depends on the observer, it cannot be an objective measure of truth; only the intrinsic truth of the proposition and the universal methods of the prophets can serve as a common scale (mizan).

Why Knowing the Universal Does Not Entail Knowing Particulars
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the claim that universal concepts can yield knowledge of particular things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's reductio ad absurdum argument against the claim that knowing a universal gives knowledge of its particulars.

Core Idea
Knowing the universal concept does not give you knowledge of any specific particular.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya responds to a hypothetical opponent who asserts that celestial souls know particulars in a particular way while intellects know them universally. He counters that knowledge of the universal – the common aspect shared by particulars – yields no knowledge of any specific particular. He supports this with concrete examples and a powerful reductio that shows the absurdity of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
Locate the phrase where the opponent says particulars are known by intellects universally and by celestial souls particularly. This sets up the target of Ibn Taymiyya's critique.
The opponent is likely representing Avicenna's position.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's first counter
Find the sentence where he states that knowledge of the universal (the shared aspect) yields no knowledge of any particular at all.
3
Examine his examples
He gives examples: knowing 'existence', 'body', 'animal', etc. does not give knowledge of any specific instance. Understand how these examples illustrate the point.
The examples are meant to be intuitive and universally understood.
4
Understand the reductio
The key argument: if particulars were known from universals, then knowing the meaning of one thing would make you know all its particulars, which is obviously false. This is a reductio ad absurdum.
The reductio targets the logical consequence of the opponent's claim.
5
Apply to the Islamic theological context
This argument directly challenges Avicenna's theory that God knows particulars in a universal way. Reflect on why this matters for Islamic theology.
This is part of the broader debate on divine omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل هم يقولون : إن الجزئياتِ معلومة للعقول على وجه كلي، وللنفوس الفلكية على وجه جزئي، قيل : العلم بالكلي - وهو القدر المشترك بين الجزئيات ـ لا يفيد العلم بشيء من الجزئيات ألبتة. فإن علم الإنسان بمسمى الوجود، أو بمسمى الجسم، أو بمسمى الحيوان أو الإنسان أو البياض، أو السواد، لا يفيده العلم بموجود معين، ولا بجسم معين ولا حيوان معين ولا إنسان معين، ولا بياض معين، ولا سواد معين. ولو كانت الجزئيات تُعلم من الكليات لكان من عَلِمَ مُسَمَّى شيءٍ قد علم كل شيء، فإنها كلها جزئيات هذا المسمى.
If it is said: They say that particulars are known by the intellects in a universal way, and by the celestial souls in a particular way. It is said: Knowledge of the universal – which is the common aspect among particulars – does not yield knowledge of any particular at all. For a person's knowledge of the meaning of existence, or the meaning of body, or the meaning of animal or human or whiteness or blackness, does not give him knowledge of a specific existent, nor a specific body, nor a specific animal, nor a specific human, nor a specific whiteness, nor a specific blackness. And if particulars were known from universals, then whoever knows the meaning of a thing would know every thing, for all things are particulars of that meaning.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage provides an objection and Ibn Taymiyya's response regarding the claim that celestial souls know particulars in a particular way while intellects know them universally. The hypothetical opponent argues that the celestial souls have particular knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya counters that knowledge of the universal (the common aspect shared by particulars) cannot yield knowledge of any specific particular. He illustrates this with examples: knowing the universal concept 'existence' does not give knowledge of any particular existent; similarly for 'body', 'animal', 'human', 'whiteness', 'blackness'. He then presents a reductio ad absurdum: if particulars were knowable through universals, then anyone who knows a universal concept would know all its particulars, which is absurd. This argument attacks the core of Avicenna's claim that God knows particulars in a universal manner – because such universal knowledge is insufficient for knowing specific individuals.

Key Terms
الكلي
الجزئيات

D) The five universals would be useless.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses a reductio ad absurdum to demonstrate that knowing a universal concept cannot give knowledge of any specific particular, thereby challenging the Peripatetic theory of knowledge.

Refuting Astrological Causation: The Uniformity Argument
Ibn Taymiyya refutes astrological causation of human thoughts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute astrological determinism using Ibn Taymiyya's uniformity argument and identify the underlying conditional syllogism.

Core Idea
If the cause is uniform, the effect must be uniform; diversity disproves causation.

Astrologers claim that celestial movements determine human thoughts and actions. Ibn Taymiyya dismantles this claim with a simple but powerful logical argument: if the cause were uniform, the effects would be uniform. Yet we observe immense diversity in human thoughts and states, even among people under the same sky. This lesson walks through his reasoning and shows how it forms a valid conditional syllogism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the astrological claim
The astrologers assert that astronomical movements (e.g., planetary aspects) cause human thoughts, beliefs, and moral states. Ibn Taymiyya focuses on the claim that the celestial configuration on a given day determines what people think and do.
2
Highlight the uniformity premise
Ibn Taymiyya notes that astronomical movements on a given day are the same for all people. If they were the cause, then all people would experience the same thoughts and states. This is a conditional: if the cause is uniform, the effect must be uniform.
3
Observe the diversity of effects
He points out that people differ: some believe, some disbelieve; some are righteous, some wicked; one person can change from believer to disbeliever without any astronomical shift. Thus the effect is not uniform.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the effect is not uniform while the claimed cause is uniform, the cause cannot be astronomical movements. This is a modus tollens syllogism: if P then Q; not Q; therefore not P.
The argument also extends to people of the same region sharing the same ascendant yet differing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك إلى مجرّد الحركات الفلكية فإن نسبة الحركة الفلكية في اليوم المعين إلى الأشخاص نسبةً واحدةً والناس مختلفون في هذه الخواطر اختلافاً لا مزيد عليه. والشخص الواحد يختلف حاله فتارةً يكون مؤمناً وتارة يكون كافراً، وتارة برا وتارةً فاجراً، وتارةً عالماً وتارة جاهلاً وتارةً ناسياً وتارةً ذاكراً، بدون حدوث سبب فلكي يرجح أحد هذين الحالين على الآخر. وأهل الأرض الواحدة، والبلد الواحد، والأقليم الواحد، تختلف أحوالهم في ذلك مع أن طالع البلد لم يختلف، ومع أن المتجدّد من الأشكال الفلكية قد يكون متشابه الأحوال وأحوالهم مع هذا تختلف. وهذا لبسطه موضع آخر. فإنّ ظن هؤلاء أن الحوادث التي تحت الفلك ليس سببها إلا تغيّر أشكال الفلك واتصالات الكواكب من أفسد الأقوال ولهذا كان أصحاب هذا القول من أكثر الناس جهلاً، وكذباً، وتناقضاً، وحيرة.
That (attribution) is to mere astronomical movements, for the ratio of the astronomical movement on a given day to individuals is one ratio, yet people differ in these thoughts with no further difference. And the single individual varies: sometimes he is a believer, sometimes a disbeliever; sometimes righteous, sometimes wicked; sometimes knowledgeable, sometimes ignorant; sometimes forgetful, sometimes mindful, without any astronomical cause that would tip one of these two states over the other. And the people of the same land, same city, same region, differ in their states in that regard, while the ascendant of the land has not changed, and while the new astronomical configurations might be similar in states, yet their states differ. This has another place for its elaboration. Indeed, the assumption of these people that events under the celestial sphere have no cause except changes in celestial configurations and planetary aspects is among the most corrupt statements. That is why the adherents of this view are among the greatest in ignorance, lying, contradiction, and confusion.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the astrological claim that human thoughts, beliefs, and moral states are caused by astronomical movements. He begins by noting that astronomical movements on a given day are uniform for all people, yet people vary immensely in their thoughts (خواطر) – some are believers, others disbelievers, etc. Moreover, the same person can change from one state to another without any corresponding astronomical shift. He then extends the argument: people of the same region share the same ascendant (طالع) and similar celestial configurations, yet their states differ. This demonstrates that astronomical factors cannot be the cause. Ibn Taymiyya declares that the belief that all sublunar events are caused only by celestial changes and planetary aspects is one of the most corrupt statements, and its adherents are among the most ignorant, contradictory, and confused people. He alludes to a longer discussion elsewhere. The argument is a straightforward empirical refutation: if the cause were uniform (astronomical movement), the effect (human states) would be uniform, but it is not, therefore the claimed causation is false.

Key Terms
الحركات الفلكية
طالع
خواطر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because astronomical movements are too weak to influence humans.
B) Because the same astronomical movement would produce uniform effects, yet people differ.
C) Because human thoughts are controlled by jinn, not stars.
D) Because the Quran forbids belief in astrology.

Key Takeaway
The uniformity of cause with diversity of effect disproves astrological causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Kaaba as a Counterexample to Astrological Determinism
Ibn Taymiyya uses the Kaaba's history to show the failure of astrologers to predict or explain its sanctity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's empirical objection to astrological determinism using the historical case of Mecca.

Core Idea
Astrology fails the test of history: the Kaaba's divine protection defies astrological prediction.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya moves from abstract critique to concrete history. He points to the Kaaba of Mecca as a glaring counterexample to astrological claims. Despite astrologers' inability to identify its 'ascendant' or predict its fate, the Kaaba has remained divinely protected for centuries. By walking through his historical examples, you will learn how to use empirical counterevidence to refute a false theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the astrologers' claim
What do astrologers believe about the fate of places? They claim that the ascendant (ṭāli‘) at the time of foundation determines the city's destiny.
The passage assumes astrologers claim to explain Mecca's honor by its ascendant.
2
Find the counterexample
Why is Mecca problematic for astrologers? Astrologers are perplexed because they cannot identify any specific ascendant that would guarantee such long-term protection and honor.
The Kaaba's history contradicts what astrological theory would predict.
3
Examine the historical evidence
Ibn Taymiyya mentions the Year of the Elephant and the siege of al-Hajjaj. In both cases, the Kaaba remained unharmed despite attacks.
He clarifies that al-Hajjaj did not target the Kaaba itself but the rebel Ibn al-Zubayr in the mosque.
4
Analyze the implication
If astrology were true, the ascendant should have predicted vulnerability. But the Kaaba was always protected. Thus, the astrological explanation fails.
The argument is an empirical falsification: the predicted outcome did not occur.
5
Evaluate the force of the argument
Does this single counterexample refute all astrology? Ibn Taymiyya uses it as a decisive refutation of astrological claims about cities and buildings.
In Islamic methodology, one solid counterexample can falsify a universal claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا حاروا في مكة - شرفها الله - وأي شيء هو الطالع الذي بنيت عليه على زعمتهم حتى رُزقت هذه السعادة العظيمة وهذا البناء العظيم مع طول الأزمان مع أنه بسوء إلا انتقم الله منه كما فعل بأصحاب الفيل، ولم يعل عليها عدوّ. لم يقصدها أحد قط إلا هلك. والحجاج بن يوسف لم يكن عدوّاً لها، ولا أراد هدمها ولا أذاها بوجه من الوجوه، ولا رماها بمَنْجَنِيق أصلاً. ولكن كان محاصراً لابن الزبير وكان ابن الزبير وأصحابه في المسجد، وكانوا يرمون بالمنجنيق له ولأصحابه، لا لقصد الكعبة. ولم يهدموا الكعبة، ولا وقع فيها شيء من حجارة الحَجّاج. بل كان ابن الزبير قد بناها على قواعد إبراهيم، وألصقها بالأرض، وجعل لها بابين كما أخبرته عائشة عن النبي ﷺ أنه قال: لولا قومك حديثوا عهد بجاهلية لنقضت الكعبة وألصقتها بالأرض وجعلتُ لها بابين - باباً يدخل الناس منه وباباً يخرجون منه. ووصف لعائشة من الحجر ما هو من البيت قريباً من سبعة أذرع موضع انحناء الحِجْر؛ وكانت قريش قد بَنتها فقَصَّرَتْ بها النفقةُ فتركوا ما تركوه من الحِجْر ورفعوها. فلما ولي ابن الزبير شارو الناس في ذلك. فمنهم من رأى ذلك مصلحة، ومنهم من أشار عليه بأن لا يفعل وقال: هذه الكعبة هي التي كانت على عهد النبي ﷺ. وعليها أسلم الناس. وهذا كان رأي ابن عباس وطائفة.
And for this reason they were perplexed about Mecca – may Allah honor it – and what is the ascendant upon which it was built, according to their claim, so that it was granted this great happiness and this great edifice over long periods of time, while if anything evil befell it, Allah took vengeance upon it, as He did with the People of the Elephant. No enemy ever rose against it. No one ever targeted it except he perished. Al-Hajjaj ibn Yusuf was not an enemy to it, nor did he intend to demolish it or harm it in any way, nor did he ever shoot at it with a catapult. Rather, he was besieging Ibn al-Zubayr, and Ibn al-Zubayr and his companions were in the mosque, and they (al-Hajjaj's forces) were shooting with the catapult at him and his companions, not aiming at the Kaaba. They did not demolish the Kaaba, nor did any of al-Hajjaj's stones fall upon it. Indeed, Ibn al-Zubayr had built it upon the foundations of Ibrahim, attached it to the ground, and made for it two doors, as 'A'isha reported from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Were it not that your people are recent in disbelief, I would have demolished the Kaaba and attached it to the ground and made for it two doors – a door for people to enter and a door for them to exit.' And he described to 'A'isha that part of the Hijr was part of the House, about seven cubits at the curve of the Hijr. The Quraysh had built it but the funds fell short, so they left what they left of the Hijr and raised it. When Ibn al-Zubayr took charge, he consulted the people about that. Some saw it as beneficial, and some advised him not to do it and said: 'This is the Kaaba that existed in the time of the Prophet ﷺ, and the people embraced Islam upon it.' This was the view of Ibn 'Abbas and a group.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of astrology, providing a concrete historical example to show the failure of astrological determinism. He points out that astrologers are perplexed about Mecca because they cannot identify the ascendant (طالع) that supposedly made it so honored and protected for centuries. Despite many attempts to harm it, such as the attack of the Abyssinian army (the Year of the Elephant), Allah destroyed the aggressors. Even the notorious governor al-Hajjaj ibn Yusuf, who besieged Mecca, did not aim at the Kaaba but at the rebel Ibn al-Zubayr inside the mosque. The Kaaba remained unharmed. Ibn Taymiyya then narrates the history of the Kaaba's construction: originally built by Ibrahim (Abraham), it was later rebuilt by the Quraysh but with a reduced size and raised door due to lack of funds. The Prophet ﷺ had expressed a desire to rebuild it on its original foundations. When Ibn al-Zubayr came to power, he consulted scholars; some supported rebuilding on the original plan, but Ibn 'Abbas and others advised against it, saying the current structure was the one under which people had embraced Islam. This shows that astrological predictions are futile, as the Kaaba's sanctity and protection are divine, not astrological.

Key Terms
طالع
الكعبة
الحَجَر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That astrologers can predict the fate of cities correctly.
B) That Mecca's sanctity is due to its favorable ascendant.
C) That astrologers are perplexed by Mecca because their theories cannot explain its divine protection.
D) That the Kaaba was rebuilt by al-Hajjaj.

Key Takeaway
Empirical counterexamples from Islamic history serve as powerful refutations (naqd) of claims that pretend to explain the world through non-divine forces like astrology.

The Praiseworthy Annihilation and the Error of the Philosophers
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes true fana' from the heretical view of Ibn Sina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the heretical elements in Ibn Sina's concept of fana' and explain Ibn Taymiyya's orthodox definition based on the shahada.

Core Idea
True annihilation is not mystical union but pure tawhid.

Ibn Taymiyya confronts the philosophical concept of spiritual annihilation (fana') as advocated by Ibn Sina and other heretics. He argues that their version is inseparably linked to multiple grave errors: denial of divine attributes, belief in the eternity of the heavens, denial of bodily resurrection, and the notion that prophethood can be attained through human effort. Against this, he presents the authentic Islamic understanding: praiseworthy annihilation is the complete realization of the testimony that there is no god but Allah, leading to exclusive worship of Him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of critique
Locate where Ibn Taymiyya names Ibn Sina and the 'malahida' as the advocates of a false fana'. Note that he considers them outside the religion of Muslims, Jews, and Christians.
2
List the heresies attributed to Ibn Sina
Extract the specific deviations mentioned: denial of attributes, eternity of heavens, denial of bodily resurrection, and the claim that prophethood is attainable through acquisition and emanation.
These are the grounds for rejecting their concept of fana'.
3
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's positive definition of fana'
Find the phrase 'al-fana' al-mahmud 'inda al-'arifin' and identify its content: it is the realization (tahqiq) of the shahada, witnessing that no created thing possesses divinity, and exclusive worship of Allah.
This definition is rooted in Quranic verses.
4
Compare the two conceptions
Contrast Ibn Sina's monistic, emanational fana' with Ibn Taymiyya's Tawhid-centric fana'. Note that for Ibn Taymiyya, the goal is not merging but purification of intention and worship.
The key difference is between pantheistic monism and strict monotheism.
5
Apply the lesson to evaluate spiritual claims
Using this passage as a criterion, assess any modern claim about spiritual annihilation: does it affirm exclusive divinity of Allah and reject all forms of shirk?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هؤلاء صاروا فِرَقاً. أما ابن سينا وأمثاله من الملاحدة فإنهم يأمرون بهذا مع سائر إلحادهم من نفي الصفات، وقدم الأفلاك، وإنكار معاد الأبدان، وجَعَلِ النبوة تُنال بالكسب كالذكاء والزهد وإنما يفيض عليها فيضُ من العقل الفعال. فيخرج من دين المسلمين واليهود والنصارى . بل الفناء المحمود عند العارفين هو تحقيق شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله . فلا يشهد لمخلوق شيئاً من الإلهية . فيشهد أنه لا خالق غيره، ويشهد أنه لا يستحق العبادة غيره، نعبد وإياك نستعين ويتحقق بحقيقة قوله: ﴿ إِيَّاكَ نَعْبُدُ وَإِيَّاكَ نَسْتَعِينُ ﴾ [سورة الفاتحة : ٥] . وقوله : فَأَعْبُدُهُ وَتَوَكَّلْ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [سورة هود ۱۲۳] .
Then these people became sects. As for Ibn Sina and his likes among the heretics, they command this along with their other heresies: denying the attributes, the eternity of the heavens, denying the resurrection of bodies, and making prophethood attainable by acquisition like intelligence and asceticism, with an emanation from the active intellect pouring upon it. So he comes out of the religion of Muslims, Jews, and Christians. Rather, the praiseworthy annihilation among the knowers is the realization of the testimony that there is no god but Allah. So he witnesses no created thing having any divinity. He witnesses that there is no creator other than Him, and he witnesses that none deserves worship other than Him. 'You alone we worship and You alone we ask for help' and it is realized by the reality of His saying: 'You alone we worship and You alone we ask for help' [Surah al-Fatiha: 5] and His saying: 'So worship Him and rely upon Him' [Surah Hud: 123].
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya contrasting the heretical philosophical conception of spiritual annihilation (fana') with the orthodox Islamic understanding. He begins by stating that the people became sects. Then he specifically targets Ibn Sina and the philosophers (the Malahida) who advocate for a state of annihilation alongside their other heresies: denial of divine attributes, belief in the eternity of the heavens, denial of bodily resurrection, and the claim that prophethood can be attained through human effort and emanations from the Active Intellect. Ibn Taymiyya declares that such a person exits the religion of the Muslims, Jews, and Christians. He then clarifies what true praiseworthy annihilation (al-fana' al-mahmud) is according to the knowers (al-'arifin): it is the realization of the shahada 'la ilaha illa Allah' – that is, witnessing that no created being shares in any aspect of divinity, that Allah alone is the Creator, and that He alone is worthy of worship. This is manifested in the verse 'You alone we worship and You alone we ask for help' (Qur'an 1:5) and 'So worship Him and rely upon Him' (Qur'an 11:123). The true fana' is thus the extinction of false objects of worship and complete devotion to Allah, not the loss of moral distinctions or a monistic merging.

Key Terms
فناء محمود
ملاحدة
شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the praiseworthy annihilation (al-fana' al-mahmud)?
A) The state where one sees all actions as coming from Allah and stops distinguishing good from evil.
B) The realization of the shahada that there is no god but Allah, and exclusive worship of Him.
C) Achieving union with the Divine through spiritual practices and knowledge.
D) Receiving emanation from the Active Intellect to gain prophethood.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that praiseworthy annihilation is not a metaphysical merging but the realization that only Allah is worthy of worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a contemporary Muslim spiritual teacher who uses the term 'fana'' and evaluate their definition according to Ibn Taymiyya's criteria: does it affirm exclusive worship of Allah? Write a short critique using the elements from this lesson.

What Is Mantiq?

10 min
Ibn Taymiyya on the Unity of Existence and the Glorification of Pharaoh
Refutation of false philosophical articles using Quranic example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the core claim of wahdat al-wujud and explain why Ibn Taymiyya considers it a rejection of Islamic principles, using his critique of Pharaoh's glorification.

Core Idea
Wahdat al-wujud leads to justifying tyranny – even Pharaoh's claim to divinity.

Ibn Taymiyya opens this section of his refutation of the philosophers by citing the Quranic story of Pharaoh to expose the dangerous implications of the monist philosophy (wahdat al-wujud). He shows how the advocates of this doctrine end up glorifying tyrants and rejecting the fundamental Islamic distinction between Creator and creation. In this lesson, we will dissect this critique and understand why Ibn Taymiyya considers such beliefs a departure from Islam altogether.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic citation
Find the verses from Surah al-Qasas (38-42) that Ibn Taymiyya quotes. Note the context: Pharaoh arrogantly claims divinity and is punished. The citation sets the stage for Ibn Taymiyya's critique.
The verses establish that Pharaoh is condemned by Allah, yet the philosophers (according to Ibn Taymiyya) praise him.
2
Extract the philosophers' interpretation of Pharaoh
Read the passage where Ibn Taymiyya says the atheists (ملاحدة) claim Pharaoh is more perfect than Moses and truthful in saying 'I am your lord most high'. Understand their reasoning: because existence is one and graded, the superior must rule the inferior.
This shows how a false metaphysical doctrine leads to a morally and theologically corrupt position.
3
Analyze the logical consequence
Consider the conclusion: if existence is one and graded, then any ruler claiming superiority could be justified. Ibn Taymiyya's point is that this doctrine destroys the basis of justice and tawhid, making it worse than polytheism.
Ibn Taymiyya later states these people are worse than many polytheists.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : مقالات للفلاسفة لم يذهب إليها أحد من المسلمين 
وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَا أَيُّهَا الْمَلَأُ مَا عَلِمْتُ لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرِي فَأَوْقِدْ لِي يَا هَامَانُ عَلَى الطِينِ فَاجْعَلْ لِي صَرْحًا لَعَلِّي أَطَّلِعُ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّهُ مِنَ الْكَذِبِينَ ) وَاسْتَكْبَرَ هُوَ وَجُنُودُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ وَظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا يُرْجَعُونَ ) فَأَخَذْنَهُ وَجُنُودَهُ فَنَبَذْنَهُمْ فِي الْبَرِّ فَانظُرْ كَيْفَ كَانَ عَقِبَةُ الظَّالِمِينَ (٥١٧) وَجَعَلْتَهُمْ أَئِمَّةٌ يَدْعُونَ إِلَى النَّارِ وَيَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ لَا يُنصَرُونَ الله وأتبعنَهُمْ فِي هَذِهِ الدُّنْيَا لَعَنَةً وَيَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ هُم مِن الْمَقْبُوحِينَ ﴾ [سورة القصص : ٣٨ - ٤٢] .
وأكثر هؤلاء الملاحدة القائلين بوحدة الوجود يقولون إن فرعون أكمل من موسى، وإن فرعون صادق في قوله «أنا ربكم الأعلى» لأن الوجود فاضل ومفضول، والفاضل يستحق أن يكون ربَّ المفضول. ومنهم من يقول: مات مؤمناً، وإن تغريقه كان ليغتسل غُسل الإسلام فإنهم مع قولهم بأن الوجود واحد قد يقولون إما بقول بعضهم: إن الثبوت غيرُ الوجود، وإن ماهيات الممكنات ثابتة، وإن وجود الحق قاض عليها، كما يقول ذلك ابن عربي وغيره؛ وإما أن يفرق بين المطلق والمعين، كما يقوله صاحبه القُونَوي؛ وابنُ سبعين قوله قريب من هذا وقد بسط الكلام عليهم في غير هذا الموضع، وإنما ذُكروا هنا لأن هؤلاء هم آخر مراتب فلاسفة الصوفية الذين يقولون إنهم أهل التحقيق والعرفان وكل من سواهم عندهم ناقص بالنسبة إليهم. وقد رأيتُ من هؤلاء غير واحد.
وهم يرتبون الناس طبقات، أدناها عندهم الفقيه، ثم المتكلم، ثم الفيلسوف، ثم الصوفي - أي صوفي الفلاسفة - ثم المحقق ويجعلون ابن سينا وأمثاله من الفلاسفة في عندهم الثانية، وأبا حامد وأمثاله من الصوفية من العشرة، ويجعلون المحقق هو الواحد.
ولهذا ذكر ابن عربي في الفتوحات له أربع عقائد الأول: عقيدة أبي المعالي وأمثاله مجردة عن الحجة، ثم هذه العقيدة بحجتها، ثم عقيدة الفلاسفة، ثم عقيدة المحققين. وذلك أن الفيلسوف يفرّق بين الوجود والممكن، والواجب، وهؤلاء يقولون «الوجود واحد». والصوفي الذي يعظمه هؤلاء هو الصوفي الذي عظمه ابن سينا. وبعده المحقق.
وهؤلاء ليسوا مسلمين ولا يهوداً ولا نصارى بل كثير من المشركين أحسن حالاً منهم.
وهؤلاء أئمة النظار المتفلسفة وصوفيتهم وشيعتهم كان من أسباب تسلطهم وظهورهم هو بِدَعُ أهل البدع من الجهمية، والمعتزلة، والرافضة، ومن نحا نحوهم في بعض الأصول الفاسدة فإن هؤلاء اشتركوا هم وأولئك الملاحدة في أصول فاسدة يجعلونها قضايا عقلية صادقة، وهي باطلة كاذبة مخالفة للشرع والعقل.
ثم أراد هؤلاء المتكلمون الردَّ عليهم في إلحادهم الظاهر الذي يظهر فيه مخالفتهم كفرهم بها للمسلمين مثل القول بقدم العالم، وإنكار علم الله بالجزئيات، والقول بإنكار المعاد. وهذه الثلاثة التي يكفّرهم بها أبو حامد الغزالي في «تهافت الفلاسفة». وطائفة يقولون: إن سائر أقوالهم الباطلة هي البدع التي ذهب إليها بعض أهل الكلام، كإنكار الصفات. وليس الأمر كما قاله هؤلاء، بل مقالاتهم التي لم يذهب إليها أحد من طوائف المسلمين - لا أهل البدعة ولا أهل السنّة - كثيرة، مثل قولهم في النبوّات، والملائكة، وكلام الله، وقولهم في الشفاعة، وإنكار مشيئة الله وقدرته. وليس هذا من لوازم القول بقدم العالم، بل في القائلين بذلك من يقول: إن الله يفعل بمشيئته وقدرته كأحد القولين الذين ذكرهما أبو البركات واختاره. وكذلك ما يقولونه في الملائكة إنها مجرد ما يتخيل في النفوس، أو إنها العقول، وإن الواحد منها أبدَعَ كل ما سواه، وإن العقل الفعّال هو المدبر لكل ما تحت الفلك، وإن الوحي على الأنبياء إنما يجيء منه، وإنه منتهى معاد الأنفس.
فإنكارهم لقدرة الله ومشيئته أعظمُ من إنكارهم لعلمه بالجزئيات. فإن كثيراً من الناس كان لا يعرف ذلك ولكن يعلم أن الله قادر خَلَق الأشياء بمشيئته، كما في الصحيحين عن ابن مسعود قال: اجتمع عند البيت ثلثة نفر - قُرَشِيّان وثَقَفي، أو ثقفيان وقرشي - كثير شحم بطونهم قليل فقه قلوبهم. فقال أحدهم: أترون الله يسمع ما نقول؟ فقال الثاني: يسمع إن جَهَرنا ولا يسمع إن أخفينا. فقال الثالث: «إن كان إذا جهرنا سمعنا فهو إذا أخفينا». فأنزل الله: ﴿وَمَا كُنتُمْ تَسْتَتِرُونَ أَن يَشْهَدَ عَلَيْكُمْ سَمْعُكُمْ﴾
The Fourth Address - The Fourteenth Aspect: Articles of the Philosophers to Which No Muslim Has Adhered. And Pharaoh said: 'O chiefs, I know not for you any god other than me. So kindle for me, O Haman, upon the clay, and make for me a tower, that I may look at the god of Moses; and indeed I think he is among the liars.' And he was arrogant, he and his soldiers, in the land without right, and they thought that they would not be returned to Us. So We seized him and his soldiers and cast them into the sea. So see what was the end of the wrongdoers. And We made them leaders calling to the Fire, and on the Day of Resurrection they will not be helped. And We caused a curse to follow them in this world, and on the Day of Resurrection they will be among the despised. (Surah al-Qasas 38-42). And most of these atheists who affirm the unity of existence say that Pharaoh is more perfect than Moses, and that Pharaoh was truthful in his statement 'I am your lord most high,' because existence is superior and inferior, and the superior deserves to be lord of the inferior. And among them are those who say he died a believer, and that his drowning was to perform the bath of Islam. For with their statement that existence is one, they may say either the statement of some of them: that 'fixedness' is other than existence, and that the quiddities of possibles are fixed, and that the existence of the Truth judges over them, as Ibn 'Arabi and others say; or they differentiate between the absolute and the particular, as his companion al-Qunawi says; and Ibn Sab'in's statement is close to this. And I have expanded the discussion about them elsewhere, and they are only mentioned here because they are the highest ranks of the Sufi philosophers who claim to be people of verification and gnosis, and everyone else is deficient relative to them. And I have seen more than one of them. And they rank people in layers, the lowest of them is the faqih, then the mutakallim, then the philosopher, then the Sufi – i.e., the Sufi of the philosophers – then the verifier. And they make Ibn Sina and his likes among the philosophers in the second rank, and Abu Hamid and his likes among the Sufis from the ten, and they make the verifier the one. And for this reason Ibn 'Arabi mentioned in his al-Futuhat four beliefs: first: the belief of Abu al-Ma'ali and his likes stripped of evidence; then this belief with its evidence; then the belief of the philosophers; then the belief of the verifiers. That is because the philosopher differentiates between existence and the possible and the necessary, while these say 'existence is one'. And the Sufi whom they venerate is the Sufi whom Ibn Sina venerated. And after him the verifier. And these are not Muslims, nor Jews, nor Christians, but many polytheists are better than them. And these – the imams of the philosophizing theoreticians and their Sufis and followers – among the causes of their dominance and appearance are the innovations of the people of innovation from the Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila, Rafida, and those who incline towards them in some corrupt principles. For these and those atheists share corrupt principles which they assume to be true rational propositions, while they are false, lying, contradictory to revelation and reason. Then these mutakallimun wanted to refute them regarding their apparent atheism which shows their opposition to the Muslims, such as the statement of the eternity of the world, the denial of God's knowledge of particulars, and the statement denying resurrection. These are the three for which Abu Hamid al-Ghazali declares them disbelievers in his 'Tahafut al-Falasifa'. And a group says that all their other false statements are the innovations which some of the people of kalam adopted, like the denial of attributes. But the matter is not as these said; rather, their articles to which no one from the groups of Muslims – neither the people of innovation nor the people of Sunnah – has adhered are many, such as their statements about prophethood, angels, the speech of God, their statement about intercession, and the denial of God's will and power. And this is not a necessary consequence of the statement of the eternity of the world; rather, among those who say that are those who say that God acts by His will and power, as one of the two statements that Abu al-Barakat mentioned and chose. And likewise what they say about angels: that they are merely what is imagined in souls, or that they are intellects, and that one of them originated everything else, and that the active intellect is the manager of everything under the sphere, and that revelation to the prophets only comes from it, and that it is the ultimate return of souls. So their denial of God's power and will is greater than their denial of His knowledge of particulars. For many people did not know that but knew that God is powerful, creating things by His will, as in the two Sahihs from Ibn Mas'ud who said: Three men gathered at the House – two Qurayshis and a Thaqafi, or two Thaqafis and a Qurayshi – much fat of their bellies, little fiqh of their hearts. One of them said: ‘Do you think God hears what we say?’ The second said: ‘He hears if we are loud, but does not hear if we are quiet.’ The third said: ‘If when we are loud He hears us, then when we are quiet He hears us.’ So God revealed: 'And you were not covering yourselves lest your hearing testify against you'.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This is a critical passage in which Ibn Taymiyya identifies and refutes the false doctrines held by the philosophers that no Muslim sect, whether orthodox or heterodox, accepts. He begins by citing the Quranic story of Pharaoh to illustrate the extreme claims of the 'atheists' (ملاحدة) who advocate the unity of existence (وحدة الوجود). These individuals assert that Pharaoh was more perfect than Moses and truthful in claiming divinity, based on a gradation of existence. Ibn Taymiyya explains that they rank people hierarchically: jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi-philosopher, and finally the 'verifier' (محقق). They consider Ibn Sina as a philosopher of the second rank, al-Ghazali as a Sufi among ten, and the verifier as the one. Ibn 'Arabi is cited for his fourfold classification of beliefs. Ibn Taymiyya then notes that such people are worse than polytheists. He attributes their influence to the innovations of groups like the Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila, and Rafida, who share corrupt principles. Moving to the philosophical articles, he states that the theologians (mutakallimun) refuted the philosophers on three major issues: eternity of the world, denial of God's knowledge of particulars, and denial of bodily resurrection – the three points for which al-Ghazali declared them disbelievers in 'Tahafut al-Falasifa'. However, Ibn Taymiyya corrects the misconception that all philosophical errors are derived from these three; instead, there are many articles that no Muslim group accepts, such as their theories on prophethood, angels (as mere imaginings or intellects), the active intellect as source of revelation, denial of God's will and power, and intercession. He emphasizes that denial of God's power is even worse than denial of His knowledge, providing a hadith about three men discussing God's hearing to illustrate innate human recognition of God's power.

Key Terms
وحدة الوجود
الملاحدة
فرعون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what do the advocates of wahdat al-wujud claim about Pharaoh?
A) Pharaoh was a disbeliever and rightly punished
B) Pharaoh was more perfect than Moses and his drowning was a ritual bath
C) Pharaoh was merely a symbol of human ambition
D) Pharaoh repented before his death

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of wahdat al-wujud leads to the absurd conclusion that Pharaoh was superior to Moses, showing how a metaphysical error can corrupt moral and theological judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What Is Mantiq?

Beyond the Three Issues: Ibn Taymiyya's Expansion of Philosophical Errors
Refutation of limitation of philosophical errors to three issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the three famous philosophical errors refuted by al-Ghazali and the many additional errors Ibn Taymiyya identifies, and explain why Ibn Taymiyya insists these are separate issues.

Core Idea
The philosophers' errors go far beyond the three points of takfir.

Ibn Taymiyya acknowledges that al-Ghazali's 'Tahafut al-Falasifa' famously declared the philosophers disbelievers on three counts: eternity of the world, denial of God's knowledge of particulars, and denial of bodily resurrection. However, in this passage, Ibn Taymiyya corrects a common misconception: he argues that the philosophers hold many other false doctrines that no Muslim group accepts, from their theories on prophethood and angels to the denial of God's will and power. This lesson will walk through this refinement, showing how Ibn Taymiyya expands the scope of criticism.

Guided Path
1
List the three famous errors from al-Ghazali
Identify the three issues mentioned in the passage that al-Ghazali used to declare the philosophers disbelievers: qidam al-'alam (eternity of the world), inkar 'ilm Allah bi al-juz'iyyat (denial of God's knowledge of particulars), and inkar al-ma'ad (denial of resurrection).
These are well-known in Islamic thought.
2
Find Ibn Taymiyya's list of additional errors
Read the passage: 'their articles to which no one from the groups of Muslims has adhered are many, such as their statements about prophethood, angels, the speech of God, their statement about intercession, and the denial of God's will and power.' Also note the specific theories about angels being mere imaginations or intellects.
Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes that these are not derived from the three errors; they are independent false doctrines.
3
Analyze why Ibn Taymiyya insists these are separate
He explicitly says 'this is not a necessary consequence of the statement of the eternity of the world' – meaning the philosophers' errors on prophethood and power are not logically entailed by the eternity claim. Each is a separate deviation.
This reinforces that the philosophers' system is corrupt at multiple points, not just a few.
