المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : مقالات للفلاسفة لم يذهب إليها أحد من المسلمين 
وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَا أَيُّهَا الْمَلَأُ مَا عَلِمْتُ لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرِي فَأَوْقِدْ لِي يَا هَامَانُ عَلَى الطِينِ فَاجْعَلْ لِي صَرْحًا لَعَلِّي أَطَّلِعُ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّهُ مِنَ الْكَذِبِينَ ) وَاسْتَكْبَرَ هُوَ وَجُنُودُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ وَظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا يُرْجَعُونَ ) فَأَخَذْنَهُ وَجُنُودَهُ فَنَبَذْنَهُمْ فِي الْبَرِّ فَانظُرْ كَيْفَ كَانَ عَقِبَةُ الظَّالِمِينَ (٥١٧) وَجَعَلْتَهُمْ أَئِمَّةٌ يَدْعُونَ إِلَى النَّارِ وَيَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ لَا يُنصَرُونَ الله وأتبعنَهُمْ فِي هَذِهِ الدُّنْيَا لَعَنَةً وَيَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ هُم مِن الْمَقْبُوحِينَ ﴾ [سورة القصص : ٣٨ - ٤٢] .
وأكثر هؤلاء الملاحدة القائلين بوحدة الوجود يقولون إن فرعون أكمل من موسى، وإن فرعون صادق في قوله «أنا ربكم الأعلى» لأن الوجود فاضل ومفضول، والفاضل يستحق أن يكون ربَّ المفضول. ومنهم من يقول: مات مؤمناً، وإن تغريقه كان ليغتسل غُسل الإسلام فإنهم مع قولهم بأن الوجود واحد قد يقولون إما بقول بعضهم: إن الثبوت غيرُ الوجود، وإن ماهيات الممكنات ثابتة، وإن وجود الحق قاض عليها، كما يقول ذلك ابن عربي وغيره؛ وإما أن يفرق بين المطلق والمعين، كما يقوله صاحبه القُونَوي؛ وابنُ سبعين قوله قريب من هذا وقد بسط الكلام عليهم في غير هذا الموضع، وإنما ذُكروا هنا لأن هؤلاء هم آخر مراتب فلاسفة الصوفية الذين يقولون إنهم أهل التحقيق والعرفان وكل من سواهم عندهم ناقص بالنسبة إليهم. وقد رأيتُ من هؤلاء غير واحد.
وهم يرتبون الناس طبقات، أدناها عندهم الفقيه، ثم المتكلم، ثم الفيلسوف، ثم الصوفي - أي صوفي الفلاسفة - ثم المحقق ويجعلون ابن سينا وأمثاله من الفلاسفة في عندهم الثانية، وأبا حامد وأمثاله من الصوفية من العشرة، ويجعلون المحقق هو الواحد.
ولهذا ذكر ابن عربي في الفتوحات له أربع عقائد الأول: عقيدة أبي المعالي وأمثاله مجردة عن الحجة، ثم هذه العقيدة بحجتها، ثم عقيدة الفلاسفة، ثم عقيدة المحققين. وذلك أن الفيلسوف يفرّق بين الوجود والممكن، والواجب، وهؤلاء يقولون «الوجود واحد». والصوفي الذي يعظمه هؤلاء هو الصوفي الذي عظمه ابن سينا. وبعده المحقق.
وهؤلاء ليسوا مسلمين ولا يهوداً ولا نصارى بل كثير من المشركين أحسن حالاً منهم.
وهؤلاء أئمة النظار المتفلسفة وصوفيتهم وشيعتهم كان من أسباب تسلطهم وظهورهم هو بِدَعُ أهل البدع من الجهمية، والمعتزلة، والرافضة، ومن نحا نحوهم في بعض الأصول الفاسدة فإن هؤلاء اشتركوا هم وأولئك الملاحدة في أصول فاسدة يجعلونها قضايا عقلية صادقة، وهي باطلة كاذبة مخالفة للشرع والعقل.
ثم أراد هؤلاء المتكلمون الردَّ عليهم في إلحادهم الظاهر الذي يظهر فيه مخالفتهم كفرهم بها للمسلمين مثل القول بقدم العالم، وإنكار علم الله بالجزئيات، والقول بإنكار المعاد. وهذه الثلاثة التي يكفّرهم بها أبو حامد الغزالي في «تهافت الفلاسفة». وطائفة يقولون: إن سائر أقوالهم الباطلة هي البدع التي ذهب إليها بعض أهل الكلام، كإنكار الصفات. وليس الأمر كما قاله هؤلاء، بل مقالاتهم التي لم يذهب إليها أحد من طوائف المسلمين - لا أهل البدعة ولا أهل السنّة - كثيرة، مثل قولهم في النبوّات، والملائكة، وكلام الله، وقولهم في الشفاعة، وإنكار مشيئة الله وقدرته. وليس هذا من لوازم القول بقدم العالم، بل في القائلين بذلك من يقول: إن الله يفعل بمشيئته وقدرته كأحد القولين الذين ذكرهما أبو البركات واختاره. وكذلك ما يقولونه في الملائكة إنها مجرد ما يتخيل في النفوس، أو إنها العقول، وإن الواحد منها أبدَعَ كل ما سواه، وإن العقل الفعّال هو المدبر لكل ما تحت الفلك، وإن الوحي على الأنبياء إنما يجيء منه، وإنه منتهى معاد الأنفس.
فإنكارهم لقدرة الله ومشيئته أعظمُ من إنكارهم لعلمه بالجزئيات. فإن كثيراً من الناس كان لا يعرف ذلك ولكن يعلم أن الله قادر خَلَق الأشياء بمشيئته، كما في الصحيحين عن ابن مسعود قال: اجتمع عند البيت ثلثة نفر - قُرَشِيّان وثَقَفي، أو ثقفيان وقرشي - كثير شحم بطونهم قليل فقه قلوبهم. فقال أحدهم: أترون الله يسمع ما نقول؟ فقال الثاني: يسمع إن جَهَرنا ولا يسمع إن أخفينا. فقال الثالث: «إن كان إذا جهرنا سمعنا فهو إذا أخفينا». فأنزل الله: ﴿وَمَا كُنتُمْ تَسْتَتِرُونَ أَن يَشْهَدَ عَلَيْكُمْ سَمْعُكُمْ﴾
The Fourth Address - The Fourteenth Aspect: Articles of the Philosophers to Which No Muslim Has Adhered. And Pharaoh said: 'O chiefs, I know not for you any god other than me. So kindle for me, O Haman, upon the clay, and make for me a tower, that I may look at the god of Moses; and indeed I think he is among the liars.' And he was arrogant, he and his soldiers, in the land without right, and they thought that they would not be returned to Us. So We seized him and his soldiers and cast them into the sea. So see what was the end of the wrongdoers. And We made them leaders calling to the Fire, and on the Day of Resurrection they will not be helped. And We caused a curse to follow them in this world, and on the Day of Resurrection they will be among the despised. (Surah al-Qasas 38-42). And most of these atheists who affirm the unity of existence say that Pharaoh is more perfect than Moses, and that Pharaoh was truthful in his statement 'I am your lord most high,' because existence is superior and inferior, and the superior deserves to be lord of the inferior. And among them are those who say he died a believer, and that his drowning was to perform the bath of Islam. For with their statement that existence is one, they may say either the statement of some of them: that 'fixedness' is other than existence, and that the quiddities of possibles are fixed, and that the existence of the Truth judges over them, as Ibn 'Arabi and others say; or they differentiate between the absolute and the particular, as his companion al-Qunawi says; and Ibn Sab'in's statement is close to this. And I have expanded the discussion about them elsewhere, and they are only mentioned here because they are the highest ranks of the Sufi philosophers who claim to be people of verification and gnosis, and everyone else is deficient relative to them. And I have seen more than one of them. And they rank people in layers, the lowest of them is the faqih, then the mutakallim, then the philosopher, then the Sufi – i.e., the Sufi of the philosophers – then the verifier. And they make Ibn Sina and his likes among the philosophers in the second rank, and Abu Hamid and his likes among the Sufis from the ten, and they make the verifier the one. And for this reason Ibn 'Arabi mentioned in his al-Futuhat four beliefs: first: the belief of Abu al-Ma'ali and his likes stripped of evidence; then this belief with its evidence; then the belief of the philosophers; then the belief of the verifiers. That is because the philosopher differentiates between existence and the possible and the necessary, while these say 'existence is one'. And the Sufi whom they venerate is the Sufi whom Ibn Sina venerated. And after him the verifier. And these are not Muslims, nor Jews, nor Christians, but many polytheists are better than them. And these – the imams of the philosophizing theoreticians and their Sufis and followers – among the causes of their dominance and appearance are the innovations of the people of innovation from the Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila, Rafida, and those who incline towards them in some corrupt principles. For these and those atheists share corrupt principles which they assume to be true rational propositions, while they are false, lying, contradictory to revelation and reason. Then these mutakallimun wanted to refute them regarding their apparent atheism which shows their opposition to the Muslims, such as the statement of the eternity of the world, the denial of God's knowledge of particulars, and the statement denying resurrection. These are the three for which Abu Hamid al-Ghazali declares them disbelievers in his 'Tahafut al-Falasifa'. And a group says that all their other false statements are the innovations which some of the people of kalam adopted, like the denial of attributes. But the matter is not as these said; rather, their articles to which no one from the groups of Muslims – neither the people of innovation nor the people of Sunnah – has adhered are many, such as their statements about prophethood, angels, the speech of God, their statement about intercession, and the denial of God's will and power. And this is not a necessary consequence of the statement of the eternity of the world; rather, among those who say that are those who say that God acts by His will and power, as one of the two statements that Abu al-Barakat mentioned and chose. And likewise what they say about angels: that they are merely what is imagined in souls, or that they are intellects, and that one of them originated everything else, and that the active intellect is the manager of everything under the sphere, and that revelation to the prophets only comes from it, and that it is the ultimate return of souls. So their denial of God's power and will is greater than their denial of His knowledge of particulars. For many people did not know that but knew that God is powerful, creating things by His will, as in the two Sahihs from Ibn Mas'ud who said: Three men gathered at the House – two Qurayshis and a Thaqafi, or two Thaqafis and a Qurayshi – much fat of their bellies, little fiqh of their hearts. One of them said: ‘Do you think God hears what we say?’ The second said: ‘He hears if we are loud, but does not hear if we are quiet.’ The third said: ‘If when we are loud He hears us, then when we are quiet He hears us.’ So God revealed: 'And you were not covering yourselves lest your hearing testify against you'.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This is a critical passage in which Ibn Taymiyya identifies and refutes the false doctrines held by the philosophers that no Muslim sect, whether orthodox or heterodox, accepts. He begins by citing the Quranic story of Pharaoh to illustrate the extreme claims of the 'atheists' (ملاحدة) who advocate the unity of existence (وحدة الوجود). These individuals assert that Pharaoh was more perfect than Moses and truthful in claiming divinity, based on a gradation of existence. Ibn Taymiyya explains that they rank people hierarchically: jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi-philosopher, and finally the 'verifier' (محقق). They consider Ibn Sina as a philosopher of the second rank, al-Ghazali as a Sufi among ten, and the verifier as the one. Ibn 'Arabi is cited for his fourfold classification of beliefs. Ibn Taymiyya then notes that such people are worse than polytheists. He attributes their influence to the innovations of groups like the Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila, and Rafida, who share corrupt principles. Moving to the philosophical articles, he states that the theologians (mutakallimun) refuted the philosophers on three major issues: eternity of the world, denial of God's knowledge of particulars, and denial of bodily resurrection – the three points for which al-Ghazali declared them disbelievers in 'Tahafut al-Falasifa'. However, Ibn Taymiyya corrects the misconception that all philosophical errors are derived from these three; instead, there are many articles that no Muslim group accepts, such as their theories on prophethood, angels (as mere imaginings or intellects), the active intellect as source of revelation, denial of God's will and power, and intercession. He emphasizes that denial of God's power is even worse than denial of His knowledge, providing a hadith about three men discussing God's hearing to illustrate innate human recognition of God's power.

إنكار علم الله بالجزئيات
إنكار المعاد
العقل الفعّال
المشيئة

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, which of the following is NOT among the articles of the philosophers that no Muslim group accepts?
A) Denial of God's will and power
B) The world is eternal
C) Angels are merely imagined forms
D) The soul is a spiritual substance

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refines the critique of the philosophers by demonstrating that their errors are far more extensive than the three famous issues, covering prophethood, angels, intercession, and divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
List the additional philosophical errors Ibn Taymiyya mentions that are not among the three famous ones. For each, specify why it is not a necessary consequence of the eternity of the world.
?
Using the same method, identify a modern intellectual movement that makes claims about prophethood or angels that no Muslim group accepts. Analyze how Ibn Taymiyya's approach would apply.

What Is Mantiq?
beginner

The Hanifas Are Muslims and the Universality of Islam
Author defines the hanifas as Muslims and asserts all prophets were Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'hanifas' based on textual evidence and explain the implication that all prophets were Muslims.

Core Idea
All prophets were Muslims; Islam is the eternal religion of submission to Allah.

In this lesson, we examine Ibn Taymiyya's definition of the 'hanifas' — the monotheistic followers of Abraham — and his assertion that they are Muslims. Through prophetic hadith and Quranic verses, he demonstrates that Islam is not a new religion but the universal path of all prophets and their followers. Understanding this definition is essential for a correct Islamic theology of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Definition
Find the phrase where Ibn Taymiyya defines who the hanifas are. Notice the description: 'those who worship Allah alone without partner.'
The definition is explicit: الحنفاء الذين يعبدون الله وحده لا شريك له.
2
Identify the Supporting Evidence
Ibn Taymiyya uses the Prophet's hadith from the Farewell Pilgrimage about conveying knowledge, and then quotes two Quranic verses (3:85 and 3:19). Identify what each piece of evidence adds to the argument.
The hadith emphasizes the duty to convey; the verses declare Islam as the only acceptable religion.
3
Extract the Logical Implication
From the definition and evidence, Ibn Taymiyya concludes that 'all the prophets and their nations were Muslims.' Identify the logical connection: if hanifas are Muslims and all prophets were hanifas, then all prophets were Muslims.
This is a straightforward deduction based on the definition.
4
Apply the Concept
Consider how this understanding affects the interpretation of Quranic verses about previous prophets. For example, Prophet Abraham is called a 'hanif' and 'Muslim' in the Quran (3:67). How does this lesson reinforce that?
This definition prevents the misconception that Islam began only with Muhammad (PBUH).

الوجه الرابع عشر: كون الحنفاء هم المسلمين. وفي الصحيحين عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال في حَجّة الوداع: «ليُبلغ الشاهد الغائب، فرُبَّ مِنْ مبلغ أوعى من سامع». والمقصود هنا أنّ الحنفاء الذين يعبدون الله وحده لا شريك له وهم مسلمون، هم المسلمين وجميع الأنبياء وأممهم كانوا مسلمين مؤمنين. ﴿ وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا فَلَن يُقْبَلَ مِنْهُ ﴾ [سورة آل عمران: 85] لأن الدِّينَ عِندَ اللهِ الْإِسْلَامُ ﴾ [سورة آل عمران: 19] ـ في كل زمان ومكان. وقد أخبر الله عن نوح وإبراهيم وإسرائيل وغيرهم إلى الحواريين أنهم كانوا مسلمين.
The fourteenth aspect: That the hanifas are the Muslims. And in the two Sahihs from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said during the Farewell Pilgrimage: 'Let the one present convey to the absent, for perhaps one who is informed is more perceptive than one who hears.' And what is intended here is that the hanifas—those who worship Allah alone without partner—are Muslims, and all the prophets and their nations were Muslims and believers. 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him' (Quran 3:85) because 'Indeed, the religion in the sight of Allah is Islam' (Quran 3:19)—in every time and place. And Allah has informed us about Noah, Abraham, Israel, and others, up to the disciples, that they were Muslims.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage defines the hanifas (the monotheistic followers of Abrahamic monotheism) as those who worship Allah alone without any partner, and it asserts that they are the Muslims. The author supports this by quoting the Prophet's hadith about conveying knowledge and then citing Quranic verses that declare Islam to be the only acceptable religion and that all prophets and their followers were Muslims. The lesson establishes the universal and timeless nature of Islam as the religion of all prophets.

مسلمون

Key Takeaway
The hanifas are Muslims who worship Allah alone, and all prophets were Muslims, making Islam the universal religion of submission to Allah.

?

?

Ibn Taymiyya’s Critique of Philosophical Shirk and Astrological Idolatry
Ibn Taymiyya critiques philosophers for shirk and their corrupt interpretation of the Mi'raj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of Ibn Taymiyya’s critique of philosophical shirk and evaluate its theological significance.

Core Idea
Philosophical monotheism can disguise actual polytheism; Ibn Taymiyya exposes the shirk in Greek-inspired cosmology.

Ibn Taymiyya does not merely reject philosophical logic; he attacks its theological consequences. In this passage, he unmasks how the doctrine of the world’s pre-eternity and astrological causation leads to explicit polytheism, even worse than that of pre-Islamic Arabs. This lesson will guide you through his critical method so you can recognize similar errors in philosophical and mystical claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Target
Determine who Ibn Taymiyya is criticizing in this passage. Look for names such as al-Razi, Ibn 'Arabi, and the philosophers (falasifa).
He also targets followers of the book 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' and the Chaldean/Cushite traditions.
2
Extract the Key Doctrines
List the central claims Ibn Taymiyya attacks: pre-eternity of the world (qidam al-‘alam), celestial causation as the only cause for events, and allegorical interpretations of the Mi'raj (e.g., prophets as planets).
These doctrines are derived from Greek philosophy and astrology.
3
Analyze the Critique
Examine how Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that these doctrines lead to shirk. He points to explicit worship of planets, jinn, and idols in al-Razi's book, and the reduction of the Mi'raj to a mental vision.
He labels this as worse than the polytheism of the pre-Islamic Arabs who at least acknowledged a Creator.
4
Evaluate the Theological Significance
Consider why Ibn Taymiyya considers philosophical shirk more dangerous: it is disguised as religion and philosophy, thus more deceptive and harder to refute without proper critique.
This shows the importance of aqidah (theology) in exposing hidden shirk.

Source Text

كتاب الرد على المنطقيين
وما فيه من الشرك
شفاعتهم موافقة للفلاسفة، كما تقدم من أن هذا القول شرّ من قول مشركي العرب (۱) . السر المكتوم وجاء بعده صاحب كتاب السرّ المكتوم في السحر ومخاطبة النجوم»(۲)، فذكر فيه الشرك الصريح من عبادة الكواكب والجن والشياطين، ودعواتها، وبَخُورها. وخواتيمها، وأصنامها التي تجعل لها على مذهب المشركين - الكلدانيين والكشدانيين - الذين بُعث إليهم إبراهيم الخليل وبَنى على ذلك القول بقدم العالم، وأن لا سبب / لحدوث الحوادث إلا مجرد حركة الفلك، كما يقوله هؤلاء القائلون بقدم العالم الذين هم شرّ من مشركي العرب.
الصريح
/ ٥٤٥
قول الرازي وكذلك ذكر في تفسير حديث المعراج ما هو مبني على أصول هؤلاء الذين هم في المعراج أكفر الكفار، كقوله إن الأنبياء الذين راهم النبي الله وهم الكواكب، «فآدم القمر، ويوسفُ الزُّهَرة»، ونحو هذا الهذيان. و : إن المعراج إنما هو رؤية قَلْبِه الوجود»، كما يذكر ابن عربي وغيره مثل هذا المعراج ويثبتون لأنفسهم إسراء ومعراجاً.
وهذه خيالات تُلقيها الشياطين مناسبة [٥٤١] لما يعتقدونه من الإلحاد على عادة كونها خيالات الشياطين في إضلال بني آدم فإنما يُضلونهم بما يَقْبَلونه منهم وما يوافق أهواءهم.
من إلقاء الشياطين
والحمد لله رب العالمين .
قال الناسخ في آخر الكتاب :
نجز على يد الفقير إلى الله تعالى محمود بن أحمد بن حسن الشافعي، غفر الله له ولوالديه ولجميع المسلمين.
وكتب في الزاوية العليا من الهامش بخط آخر :
بلغت مقابلة بأصل المصنف بخطه المقروء عليه رضي الله عنه في سنة ثمان وعشرين وسبع مئة في سبع ذي الحجة وقد قرأت عليه أوائل هذه النسخة وكتب بخطه على هوامشها زيادات له تمم. . . . . قرأت . . . النسخة
The Book of Refutation against the Logicians
And what is in it of polytheism
Their intercession is agreement with the philosophers, as has preceded that this statement is worse than the statement of the polytheists of the Arabs (1). The Hidden Secret. And after him came the author of the book 'The Hidden Secret' on sorcery and addressing the stars (2), so he mentioned in it explicit polytheism from the worship of planets, jinn, and devils, and their incantations, their incense, their seals, and their idols which they set up according to the doctrine of the polytheists - the Chaldeans and the Cushites - to whom Abraham the Friend was sent, and he built upon that the statement of the pre-eternity of the world, and that there is no cause for the occurrence of events except mere movement of the sphere, as those who say the world is pre-eternal - who are worse than the polytheists of the Arabs - say.
The explicit
/ 545
Statement of al-Razi. Likewise he mentioned in his commentary on the hadith of the Mi'raj what is based on the principles of those who in the Mi'raj are the most disbelieving of the disbelievers, such as his statement that the prophets whom the Prophet of God saw are the planets, 'So Adam is the moon, and Joseph is Venus,' and similar nonsense. And: 'The Mi'raj is only a vision of his heart of existence,' as Ibn 'Arabi and others mention such a Mi'raj and affirm for themselves an Isra' and Mi'raj.
And these are fantasies that the devils cast, suitable [541?] for what they believe of atheism, in the manner of devils' fantasies in misleading the children of Adam; they only mislead them by what they accept from them and what agrees with their desires.
From the casting of the devils
And praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
The copyist said at the end of the book:
It was completed by the hand of the poor to God Almighty Mahmud ibn Ahmad ibn Hasan al-Shafi'i, may God forgive him and his parents and all Muslims.
And written in the upper corner of the margin by another hand:
It was collated with the original of the author in his own handwriting, read to him, may God be pleased with him, in the year 728, on the 7th of Dhu al-Hijjah, and I read the beginnings of this copy, and he wrote in his handwriting on its margins additions that he completed... I read... the copy.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya against philosophers and those influenced by them. He begins by stating that the intercession of these groups aligns with the philosophers, and their statement is worse than that of the Arab polytheists. He then references the book 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' (The Hidden Secret), attributing it to al-Razi, which contains explicit polytheism: worship of planets, jinn, devils, incantations, incense, seals, and idols according to the way of the Chaldeans and Cushites, to whom Prophet Abraham was sent. Ibn Taymiyya points out that this belief is built on the doctrine of the pre-eternity of the world, where causes of events are reduced to mere celestial movements. He contrasts this with the polytheists of the Arabs, considering the philosophers even worse. Next, he attacks al-Razi's commentary on the hadith of the Mi'raj (the Prophet's ascension), where al-Razi claims that the prophets seen by the Prophet are actually planets (Adam as the moon, Joseph as Venus) — a statement Ibn Taymiyya calls 'hudhayyan' (nonsense). Ibn Taymiyya also criticizes the notion that the Mi'raj is merely a vision of the heart of existence, as claimed by Ibn 'Arabi and others, who falsely claim an Isra' and Mi'raj for themselves. He labels these as fantasies cast by devils, designed to mislead people by appealing to their desires. The passage ends with the copyist's colophon noting the completion and collation. Ibn Taymiyya's critique is sharp: he sees these philosophical and mystical interpretations as not merely erroneous but as shirk (polytheism) and atheism, more dangerous than the idolatry of pre-Islamic Arabs because they are disguised as religion and philosophy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in this passage, what makes the philosophers' position worse than the polytheism of the pre-Islamic Arabs?
A) They reject all forms of worship.
B) They base their beliefs on the pre-eternity of the world and celestial causation, leading to explicit polytheism.
C) They deny the existence of prophets.
D) They advocate for the worship of idols openly.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya’s critique reveals that philosophical systems, when based on pre-eternity and astral causation, inevitably lead to shirk, making them more dangerous than outright idolatry because they are disguised as rationalism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read an excerpt from al-Razi's 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' (if available) and identify the elements Ibn Taymiyya would consider shirk. Write a short analysis.
?
Consider a contemporary allegorical interpretation of a prophetic event (e.g., the splitting of the moon). Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, argue whether it leads to shirk or preserves tawhid.
